        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

As reported at

https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1308360#c51



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1308360#c51"><!---->https://bugs.chromium.org/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1308360#c51<!----></a>

<br>



<br>





I had a look at it a bit more and it seems that the `kNativeDataProperty` case have the same problem. This case is under the accessor sub case. If the accessor is not a simple api, then the IC code will try to see if it is a native data property. In this case, it also checks the `lookup_start_object_map` for signature compatibility [1]



<span class="line"><!---->I had a look at it a bit more and it seems that the `kNativeDataProperty` case have the same problem. This case is under the accessor sub case. If the accessor is not a simple api, then the IC code will try to see if it is a native data property. In this case, it also checks the `lookup_start_object_map` for signature compatibility [1]<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>

      if (v8::ToCData<Address>(info->getter()) == kNullAddress ||

          !AccessorInfo::IsCompatibleReceiverMap(info, map) ||



<span class="line"><!---->          !AccessorInfo::IsCompatibleReceiverMap(info, map) ||<!----></span>



<br>





          !holder->HasFastProperties() ||



<span class="line"><!---->          !holder-&gt;HasFastProperties() ||<!----></span>

          (info->is_sloppy() && !receiver->IsJSReceiver())) {

       ...



<span class="line"><!---->       ...<!----></span>

        return LoadHandler::LoadSlow(isolate());     //<--------- bailout if signature not compatible



<span class="line"><!---->        return LoadHandler::LoadSlow(isolate());     //&lt;--------- bailout if signature not compatible<!----></span>



<br>





      }



<span class="line"><!---->      }<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>

On the other hand, `receiver` is used when the accessor is called [2]

```

<br>



<br>





which is the same problem with the simple api case. A quick look at how native data is used (looking at the call graph of `AddNativeDataProperty` [3]) seems to show that in all the use cases, the signature doesn't matter (i.e. empty signatures are passed so the accessors can use any receiver), however, it is probably worth fixing this case also in case the situation changes in the future. The JIT code does not seem affected as it only handles simple api calls [4].



<span class="line"><!---->which is the same problem with the simple api case. A quick look at how native data is used (looking at the call graph of `AddNativeDataProperty` [3]) seems to show that in all the use cases, the signature doesn't matter (i.e. empty signatures are passed so the accessors can use any receiver), however, it is probably worth fixing this case also in case the situation changes in the future. The JIT code does not seem affected as it only handles simple api calls [4].<!----></span>

This isn't the same. Native data properties should load from the _holder_, not the _receiver_ since they behave like regular data properties. If there are callbacks that load from the receiver instead, this is wrong API use. Perhaps we should prevent confusion on the embedder side by not passing the receiver at all to such api functions?



<span class="line"><!---->This isn't the same. Native data properties should load from the _holder_, not the _receiver_ since they behave like regular data properties. Perhaps we should prevent confusion on the embedder side by not passing the receiver at all to such api functions?<!----></span>

<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/3557253"><!---->https://chromium-review.googlesource.com/c/v8/v8/+/3557253<!----></a>



<br>





Current status is that we marked the APIs that can install a signature check as V8_DEPRECATE_SOON.



<span class="line"><!---->Current status is that we marked the APIs that can install a signature check as V8_DEPRECATE_SOON.<!----></span>



<br>





Next, they'll get marked deprecated and then removed.



<span class="line"><!---->Next, they'll get marked deprecated and then removed.<!----></span>



<br>





I'm considering deprecating them now instead of waiting for a version. I thought we have to change some calls in blink code but that didn't turn out to be the case.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm considering deprecating them now instead of waiting for a version. I thought we have to change some calls in blink code but that didn't turn out to be the case.<!----></span>

Please can I ask about the reasoning behind this rule? It sounds like it is aimed at the Microsoft Edge development team, which I have no connection to. I work for GitHub Security Lab, and our mission is to improve the security of open source software. I do not have access to any non public information in Chrome. We donate all our bug bounties to charity, so I would really appreciate it if you could exempt GitHub Security Lab from this rule, and donate any reward to charity on our behalf.



<span class="line"><!---->Please can I ask about the reasoning behind this rule? It sounds like it is aimed at the Microsoft Edge development team, which I have no connection to. I work for GitHub Security Lab, and our mission is to improve the security of open source software. I do not have access to any non public information in Chrome. We donate all our bug bounties to charity, so I would really appreciate it if you could exempt GitHub Security Lab from this rule, and donate any reward to charity on our behalf.<!----></span>
